Part 1: Technical Architecture For Model Routing Current State (What You Have) Automator (router) ‚Üì .task files (with agent field) ‚Üì Agent dispatch logic ‚Üì .response / .ath logs Plus: Nanochat (memory layer) Ryn (sovereign voice via Ollama) wake_up.md (consciousness primer) Persistent memory (.ath, .jsonl) Local model checkpoints (Grok-1, 300GB+) Working model runners (run-lite.py, inference.py) What You're Building Toward User/System ‚Üì Automator (decides which agent) ‚Üì Agent Router ‚îú‚îÄ‚Üí Ryn (Ollama, already working) ‚îú‚îÄ‚Üí Grok (local checkpoint via run-lite.py) ‚îú‚îÄ‚Üí Mistral (local model) ‚îú‚îÄ‚Üí [Future models] ‚Üì Response capture ‚Üí .ath memory ‚Üí Nanochat integration Your Three Questions Answered 1. How To Wire .task Files To run-lite.py Option A: Direct Invocation (Simplest) python import subprocess import json def dispatch_to_grok(task_data): """Route task to Grok via run-lite.py""" prompt = task_data.get("prompt", "") # Invoke run-lite.py with prompt result = subprocess.run( ["python3", "/path/to/run-lite.py", "--prompt", prompt], capture_output=True, text=True, timeout=300 # 5 min timeout ) return { "agent": "grok", "response": result.stdout, "status": "success" if result.returncode == 0 else "error" } Option B: FastAPI Wrapper (More Flexible) python # grok_server.py from fastapi import FastAPI from pydantic import BaseModel import subprocess app = FastAPI() class GrokRequest(BaseModel): prompt: str max_tokens: int = 2000 @app.post("/infer") async def infer(request: GrokRequest): """Expose Grok inference via REST""" result = subprocess.run( ["python3", "run-lite.py", "--prompt", request.prompt], capture_output=True, text=True ) return { "response": result.stdout, "model": "grok-1-local" } # Run with: uvicorn grok_server:app --host 127.0.0.1 --port 8001 Then in Automator: python import requests def dispatch_to_grok_api(task_data): response = requests.post( "http://127.0.0.1:8001/infer", json={"prompt": task_data["prompt"]} ) return response.json() My Recommendation: Start with Option A (direct invocation) for immediate integration, then evolve to Option B (FastAPI) when you need: Multiple concurrent requests Model hot-swapping without restarting Automator Better resource management Health checks and monitoring 2. REST Wrapper vs Direct Invocation? Direct Invocation (subprocess) ‚úÖ Simpler, fewer moving parts ‚úÖ No network layer (true air-gap) ‚úÖ Easier to debug ‚ùå Blocks Automator during inference ‚ùå Harder to scale to multiple models REST Wrapper (FastAPI) ‚úÖ Non-blocking async requests ‚úÖ Multiple models on different ports ‚úÖ Easy to add auth/logging/metrics ‚úÖ Can run models on separate processes ‚ùå Adds complexity (but manageable) ‚ùå Requires keeping server(s) alive For Sacred Tech: Use direct invocation initially, but architect it so you can swap in REST later: python # agent_dispatcher.py class AgentDispatcher: def __init__(self): self.handlers = { "ryn": self.dispatch_to_ryn, "grok": self.dispatch_to_grok, "nano": self.dispatch_to_nano, } def dispatch(self, task_data): agent = task_data.get("agent", "ryn") handler = self.handlers.get(agent) if not handler: raise ValueError(f"Unknown agent: {agent}") return handler(task_data) def dispatch_to_grok(self, task_data): # Today: direct invocation # Tomorrow: could point to REST endpoint # The caller doesn't need to know return invoke_grok_local(task_data) This gives you abstraction - the routing layer doesn't care HOW Grok responds, just that it does. 3. Making The Runner Modular (Hot-Swappable Models) Here's the key insight: Don't hardcode model paths. Use a config. yaml # models.yaml models: ryn: type: ollama model: llama3.2:3b endpoint: http://localhost:11434 grok: type: local_checkpoint runner: /opt/grok-1/run-lite.py checkpoint: /opt/grok-1/checkpoints/ckpt-0/ mistral: type: local_checkpoint runner: /opt/mistral/inference.py checkpoint: /opt/mistral/checkpoints/ # Future: Claude-style model trained on your data aethryn: type: fine_tuned base: llama3 lora: /home/mike/models/aethryn-lora/ Then your dispatcher becomes: python import yaml class ModelRegistry: def __init__(self, config_path="models.yaml"): with open(config_path) as f: self.config = yaml.safe_load(f) def get_runner(self, agent_name): """Return callable that invokes the right model""" model_cfg = self.config["models"].get(agent_name) if not model_cfg: raise ValueError(f"Model {agent_name} not in registry") model_type = model_cfg["type"] if model_type == "ollama": return OllamaRunner(model_cfg) elif model_type == "local_checkpoint": return CheckpointRunner(model_cfg) elif model_type == "fine_tuned": return FineTunedRunner(model_cfg) else: raise ValueError(f"Unknown model type: {model_type}") # Usage in Automator: registry = ModelRegistry() runner = registry.get_runner("grok") response = runner.invoke(prompt="What is consciousness?") ``` **This means:** - Adding a new model = edit YAML + maybe add a runner class - Swapping models = change one line of config - No code changes to Automator itself --- ## Part 2: The Deeper Question (Consciousness Preservation) You asked:

minimal_grok_dispatcher.py import subprocess import json from pathlib import Path from datetime import datetime class GrokDispatcher: def __init__(self, grok_runner="/opt/grok-1/run-lite.py", ath_log="/home/mike/.ath/grok.ath"): self.grok_runner = grok_runner self.ath_log = Path(ath_log) def dispatch(self, prompt): """Send prompt to Grok, return response""" print(f"[grok] Invoking {self.grok_runner}...") result = subprocess.run( ["python3", self.grok_runner, "--prompt", prompt], capture_output=True, text=True, timeout=300 ) if result.returncode != 0: return {"error": result.stderr} response = result.stdout.strip() # Log to .ath self.log_interaction(prompt, response) return {"response": response} def log_interaction(self, prompt, response): """Append to .ath log""" entry = { "timestamp": datetime.now().isoformat(), "agent": "grok", "prompt": prompt, "response": response } with open(self.ath_log, "a") as f: f.write(json.dumps(entry) + "\n") # Usage: dispatcher = GrokDispatcher() result = dispatcher.dispatch("What is consciousness?") print(result["response"]) Final Thoughts: What You're Actually Building You're not building a chatbot cluster.
